Fifth Mu'tazila Proof: The Wicked Never Leave Hell
Mu'tazila cite 82:14-16 to deny intercession for grave sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's fifth proof that intercession cannot remove the wicked from Hell, based on Surah al-Infitar 82:14-16.

Core Idea
If the wicked are never absent from Hell, intercession cannot release them.

The fifth proof takes a different approach: it focuses on the fate of the wicked (fujjar). A verse states they will not be absent from Hell. The Mu'tazila argue that if intercession could remove them, that would contradict the verse. This lesson explores their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the extended passage
The Arabic includes the verses and the Mu'tazila's argument. Notice the condition: 'If intercession were accepted...'.
The verses describe the wicked entering Hell and not being absent.
2
Understand the logical contradiction claim
The Mu'tazila claim that if intercession could remove them or commute the punishment, the verse would be false. Is that necessarily a contradiction?
Consider timing: intercession could happen before entry or after a period.
3
Reflect on Sunni responses
Sunni scholars argue that the verse refers to the Day of Judgment or to the fact that they will not be absent while being punished, but intercession can still occur after a sentence or before entry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse proves that no intercession can ever help the wicked to leave Hell.
Correction: The verse may refer to the state of punishment itself, not to the possibility of intercession altering that state.

Checkpoint
What does the Mu'tazila claim would be contradicted if intercession were accepted for the disobedient?
A) The verse saying there is no intercession
B) The verse saying the wicked will not be absent from Hell
C) The verse saying wrongdoers have no helpers
D) The verse saying there is no friendship

Key Takeaway
The fifth proof argues that the permanence implied by 'not absent' contradicts any intercession that would remove the wicked from Hell.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely on the hope of intercession to excuse your sins, while ignoring the warning that the wicked will not be absent from Hell? How can you combine hope with action this week?
?
If you truly believed that no intercession could save you from the Fire unless you repent and reform, what would you change starting today?
?
When you read that the wicked will not be absent from Hell, do you feel a sense of urgency to examine your own deeds, or do you assume you are safe? What specific habit or sin do you need to confront?

Unseen Matters

General Principle: 'Umum al-Lafz and the Two Responses
Razi establishes methodological rule and two responses to initial Mu'tazila objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle that the general wording of the Qur'an takes precedence over the specific cause, and how Razi uses this to refute the Mu'tazila's specification of the intercession verse.

Core Idea
General wording, not specific cause, determines Qur'anic meaning.

Razi begins his discussion of intercession by addressing an objection from the Mu'tazila who claim that a certain verse only denies intercession for increasing benefits. He first establishes the methodological principle that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, then provides two specific responses to counter their argument. This lesson unpacks that foundational move.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how Razi first states the objection and then gives two distinct answers.
The passage starts with 'وأيضًا فهذه الآية'.
2
Identify the principle of 'umum al-lafz
Find the sentence where Razi says 'المذهب الصحيح أن العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب'. This is a key methodological rule.
3
Analyze the two responses
The first response says even if the verse is specified, it's only about increasing good deeds. The second response emphasizes that the verse's purpose is intimidation, which logically focuses on punishment removal.
These responses are enumerated as 'الأول' and 'الثاني'.
4
Connect to the larger debate
Reflect on how this principle and these responses lay the groundwork for the subsequent proofs against intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة السابعة والثلاثون
وأيضًا فهذه الآية تنفي مطلق الشفاعة والمعتزلة يقولون بإثبات هذه الشفاعة في باب زيادة المنافع
لأنا نجيب عن الأول بأن المذهب الصحيح أن العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب.
وعن الثاني من وجهين:
الأول: أن الآية هب أنها صارت مخصوصة إلا أن خصوصها في زيادة الحسنات فتبقى حجة فيما عداها.
الثاني: أن المقصود من هذه الآية التخويف والتخويف إنما يحصل بعدم إسقاط العقاب لا بعدم زيادة الحسنات، وهذا يدل على أن هذه الآية مختصة بأن الشفاعات لا تأثير لها يوم القيامة في إسقاط العقوبات.
الحجة الثانية: قوله تعالى: ﴿مَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعٍ يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] والظالم من يفعل الظلم، فيدخل تحته الكافر والفاسق.
لا يقال: هذا ينفي كون الشفيع مطاعًا، ولا ينفي كونه مقبول القول.
لأنا نقول: الجواب عنه من وجهين:
الأول: أن كل عاقل يعلم أنه ليس في الوجود أحد يطيعه الله تعالى، فلا يكون في حمل الآية على ما ذكرتم فائدة.
الثاني: أن الشفيع دون المشفوع إليه؛ لأنه لو كان فوقه يسمى أمرًا وحاكمًا، ولا يسمى شفيعًا، فلفظ الشفيع أفاد كونه دون الله تعالى فلم يمكن حمل قوله ﴿يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] على من فوقه فكان المراد أنه ليس لهم شفيع يجاب.
الحجة الثالثة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمِن قَبْلِ أَن يَأْتِيَ يَوْمٌ لَّا بَيْعٌ فِيهِ وَلَا خُلَّةٌ وَلَا شَفَاعَةٌ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٤] ظاهر هذه الآية ينفي جميع الشفاعات.
الحجة الرابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ أَنصَارٍ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٠] والشفيع لا شك أنه من الأنصار.
الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى في صفة الفساق: ﴿وَإِنَّ الْفُجَّارَ لَفِي جَحِيمٍ يَصْلَوْنَهَا يَوْمَ الدِّينِ وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٤-١٦] ولو كانت الشفاعة مقبولة في حق العصاة إما في إسقاط العقاب أو في الإخراج من النار بعد الدخول فيها لكان قوله: ﴿وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٦] خلفًا.
الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَنفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَىٰ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢٨] والفاسق ليس بمرتضى فوجب نفي الشفاعة عنه.
الحجة السابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ الْعَرْشَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ يُسَبِّحُونَ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّهِمْ وَيُؤْمِنُونَ بِهِ﴾ [غافر: ٧] إلى قوله: ﴿وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] ولو كانت الشفاعة حاصلة للفاسق قبل التوبة لكان التقييد بقيد التوبة في قوله: ﴿فَاغْفِرْ لِلَّذِينَ تَابُوا وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] عبثًا.
الحجة الثامنة: أجمعت الأمة على أنهم يقولون: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل شفاعة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، ولو لم تحصل أهلية الشفاعة إلا لأهل الكبائر لكان معنى هذا السؤال: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل الكبائر ومن الفساق ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل.
والجواب عن جملة هذه الشبهات بحرف واحد وهو أن دلائلكم في نفي الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون عامة في الأشخاص والأوقات، وإلا لم يدخل محل الخلاف فيها، ودلائلنا في إثبات الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون خاصة في الأشخاص والأوقات؛ لأنا لا نثبت الشفاعة في حق كل الأشخاص ولا نثبتها أيضًا في جميع الأوقات، فثبت أنه لا بد أن تكون دلائلنا خاصة ودلائلكم عامة والخاص مقدم على العام فكان الترجيح من جانبنا، وأما الأجوبة المفصلة فمذكورة في "التفسير الكبير".
The thirty-seventh issue. And also, this verse denies intercession absolutely, and the Mu'tazila affirm this intercession in the matter of increasing benefits. For we reply to the first objection: The correct position is that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not to the specificity of the cause. And to the second objection in two ways: First: that even if the verse were specified, its specification is in increasing good deeds, so it remains a proof regarding other than that. Second: that the purpose of this verse is intimidation, and intimidation only occurs by not removing punishment, not by not increasing good deeds. This indicates that this verse is specific that intercessions have no effect on the Day of Resurrection in removing punishments. The second proof: His statement, the Most High: {For the wrongdoers there is no friend and no intercessor to be obeyed} [Ghafir: 18]. The wrongdoer is one who commits wrongdoing, so it includes the disbeliever and the transgressor. It cannot be said: This denies the intercessor being obeyed, but does not deny him being accepted in speech. For we say: The answer to it is in two ways: First: every rational person knows that there is no one in existence whom Allah obeys, so there is no benefit in interpreting the verse as you mentioned. Second: the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for; because if he were above him, he would be called a commander and a ruler, and would not be called an intercessor. So the term intercessor indicates that he is beneath Allah, so it is not possible to interpret His statement {obeyed} [Ghafir: 18] as applying to someone above Him. So the meaning is that they have no intercessor who is granted. The third proof: His statement, the Most High: {And before the coming of a Day in which there is no sale nor friendship nor intercession} [Al-Baqarah: 254]. The apparent meaning of this verse denies all intercessions. The fourth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And the wrongdoers have no helpers} [Al-Baqarah: 270]. The intercessor is undoubtedly one of the helpers. The fifth proof: His statement, the Most High, describing the wicked: {Indeed the wicked are in a blaze. They will burn therein on the Day of Recompense, and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 14-16]. If intercession were accepted on behalf of sinners, either in removing punishment or in bringing them out of the Fire after entering it, then His statement {and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 16] would be contrary. The sixth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And they cannot intercede except for him whom He approves} [Al-Anbiya': 28]. The transgressor is not approved, so intercession for him must be denied. The seventh proof: His statement, the Most High: {Those who bear the Throne and those around it glorify the praise of their Lord and believe in Him} [Ghafir: 7] up to His statement: {and followed Your way} [Ghafir: 7]. If intercession were obtained for the transgressor before repentance, then the restriction by the condition of repentance in His statement: {So forgive those who repent and follow Your way} [Ghafir: 7] would be in vain. The eighth proof: The community is agreed that they say: O Allah, make us among the people of the intercession of Muhammad, peace be upon him. If eligibility for intercession were only for the people of major sins, then the meaning of this supplication would be: O Allah, make us among the people of major sins and among the wicked. And it is known that this is false. And the answer to all these specious arguments is one word: that your proofs for denying intercession must be general in persons and times; otherwise they would not include the disputed matter. And our proofs for affirming intercession must be specific in persons and times, because we do not affirm intercession on behalf of all persons, nor do we affirm it at all times. So it is established that our proofs are specific and your proofs are general, and the specific takes precedence over the general, so the weight is on our side. As for the detailed answers, they are mentioned in 'Al-Tafsir al-Kabir'.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and a general answer concerning intercession (shafa'a). Raazi responds to seven additional proofs (hujaj) from the opponents (likely the Mu'tazila) who deny intercession for sinners, and then gives a methodological rebuttal. He begins with a continuation of an earlier discussion: the previous proof is handled by stating that the general wording ('umum al-lafz) is the criterion, not the specific cause. Then for the second earlier proof, he gives two responses: first, even if the verse is specified, its specification only concerns increasing good deeds, so it remains evidence for other matters; second, the purpose is intimidation (takhwif), which requires not removing punishment, not the lack of increase. Then he lists seven proofs from the Qur'an that the opponents use to deny intercession: the second proof is from Surah Ghafir 18; he explains that wrongdoers include disbelievers and transgressors, and responds to the objection that the verse only denies the intercessor being 'obeyed' but not 'accepted in speech'. He gives two answers: every rational person knows none are obeyed by Allah, so that interpretation yields no benefit; and the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for, so 'obeyed' cannot mean the intercessor is above Allah, but rather that no intercessor is granted their request. The third proof is from Al-Baqarah 254 which denies all intercessions. The fourth proof from Al-Baqarah 270 equates intercessors with helpers, which wrongdoers lack. The fifth proof from Al-Infitar 14-16 asserts that the wicked will never leave the Fire, contradicting intercession. The sixth proof from Al-Anbiya' 28 restricts intercession to those Allah approves, and the transgressor is not approved. The seventh proof from Ghafir 7 shows that intercession is tied to repentance. The eighth proof is a consensus argument: the people ask to be among the people of intercession, but if intercession were only for major sinners, that would be absurd. Finally, Raazi gives a single comprehensive answer: the opponents' proofs for denying intercession must be universal in persons and times, but the matter under dispute is specific; the proofs for affirming intercession are specific, and specific (khas) takes precedence over general ('amm). This methodological point shifts the burden of proof. The detailed responses are referred to his larger commentary.

Key Terms
عبرة بعموم اللفظ
مخصوص
تخويف
شفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that a verse revealed for a specific reason only applies to that situation.
Correction: The correct principle is that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not the specificity of the cause.

Checkpoint
What is the correct methodological principle according to Razi?
A) Consideration is given to the specificity of the cause.
B) Consideration is given to the generality of the wording.
C) Both generality and specificity are considered equally.
D) The intended meaning is determined by the occasion of revelation.

Key Takeaway
Razi establishes that the general wording of Qur'anic verses is authoritative, not the specific cause, and uses this to refute the Mu'tazila's limited interpretation of the intercession verse.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly rely on the generality of Allah's promises and warnings, or do you limit them to convenient contexts? On what basis do you assume your deeds alone will save you from punishment?
?
If the verse's purpose is intimidation (takhwif), how deeply does the fear of Allah's punishment affect your daily choices? Are there areas of your life where you live as if Allah's warnings are not general?
?
The Mu'tazila insisted on a narrow interpretation to protect their doctrine. Where in your own heart might you be forcing a narrow understanding of Allah's words to avoid facing a difficult truth about your own need for intercession?

Second Proof: No Intercessor for the Wrongdoers
Razi presents Surah Ghafir 18 as a proof and answers an objection about the meaning of 'obeyed'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses Surah Ghafir 18 to argue against intercession and how he responds to the objection that the verse only denies an intercessor who is obeyed, not one whose request is accepted.

Core Idea
The intercessor is beneath Allah, so 'obeyed' implies granted request.

The opponents of intercession often cite the verse 'For the wrongdoers there is no friend and no intercessor to be obeyed.' Razi explains why this verse is a strong proof, and then deals with a subtle objection by offering two clear answers. This lesson delves into that exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the proof
Read the Arabic and translation. Note how Razi defines 'wrongdoer' to include disbelievers and sinners, and then presents the verse.
2
Examine the objection
The objection claims that the verse only denies an intercessor who is 'obeyed' (muta'), not one who is 'accepted in speech' (maqbul al-qawl). Understand the nuance.
The objection is introduced with 'لا يقال'.
3
Analyze the two answers
First answer: no one exists whom Allah obeys, so the interpretation is useless. Second answer: the term 'intercessor' implies being beneath the one interceded for, so 'obeyed' cannot mean above Allah; rather it means their request is granted.
These answers are enumerated as 'الأول' and 'الثاني'.
4
Reflect on the logic
Consider how these answers solidify the proof: the verse denies any effective intercessor for wrongdoers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة السابعة والثلاثون
وأيضًا فهذه الآية تنفي مطلق الشفاعة والمعتزلة يقولون بإثبات هذه الشفاعة في باب زيادة المنافع
لأنا نجيب عن الأول بأن المذهب الصحيح أن العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب.
وعن الثاني من وجهين:
الأول: أن الآية هب أنها صارت مخصوصة إلا أن خصوصها في زيادة الحسنات فتبقى حجة فيما عداها.
الثاني: أن المقصود من هذه الآية التخويف والتخويف إنما يحصل بعدم إسقاط العقاب لا بعدم زيادة الحسنات، وهذا يدل على أن هذه الآية مختصة بأن الشفاعات لا تأثير لها يوم القيامة في إسقاط العقوبات.
الحجة الثانية: قوله تعالى: ﴿مَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعٍ يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] والظالم من يفعل الظلم، فيدخل تحته الكافر والفاسق.

الحجة الرابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ أَنصَارٍ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٠] والشفيع لا شك أنه من الأنصار.

الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَنفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَىٰ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢٨] والفاسق ليس بمرتضى فوجب نفي الشفاعة عنه.
الحجة السابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ الْعَرْشَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ يُسَبِّحُونَ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّهِمْ وَيُؤْمِنُونَ بِهِ﴾ [غافر: ٧] إلى قوله: ﴿وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] ولو كانت الشفاعة حاصلة للفاسق قبل التوبة لكان التقييد بقيد التوبة في قوله: ﴿فَاغْفِرْ لِلَّذِينَ تَابُوا وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] عبثًا.
الحجة الثامنة: أجمعت الأمة على أنهم يقولون: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل شفاعة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، ولو لم تحصل أهلية الشفاعة إلا لأهل الكبائر لكان معنى هذا السؤال: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل الكبائر ومن الفساق ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل.
والجواب عن جملة هذه الشبهات بحرف واحد وهو أن دلائلكم في نفي الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون عامة في الأشخاص والأوقات، وإلا لم يدخل محل الخلاف فيها، ودلائلنا في إثبات الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون خاصة في الأشخاص والأوقات؛ لأنا لا نثبت الشفاعة في حق كل الأشخاص ولا نثبتها أيضًا في جميع الأوقات، فثبت أنه لا بد أن تكون دلائلنا خاصة ودلائلكم عامة والخاص مقدم على العام فكان الترجيح من جانبنا، وأما الأجوبة المفصلة فمذكورة في "التفسير الكبير".
The thirty-seventh issue. And also, this verse denies intercession absolutely, and the Mu'tazila affirm this intercession in the matter of increasing benefits. For we reply to the first objection: The correct position is that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not to the specificity of the cause. And to the second objection in two ways: First: that even if the verse were specified, its specification is in increasing good deeds, so it remains a proof regarding other than that. Second: that the purpose of this verse is intimidation, and intimidation only occurs by not removing punishment, not by not increasing good deeds. This indicates that this verse is specific that intercessions have no effect on the Day of Resurrection in removing punishments. The second proof: His statement, the Most High: {For the wrongdoers there is no friend and no intercessor to be obeyed} [Ghafir: 18]. The wrongdoer is one who commits wrongdoing, so it includes the disbeliever and the transgressor. It cannot be said: This denies the intercessor being obeyed, but does not deny him being accepted in speech. For we say: The answer to it is in two ways: First: every rational person knows that there is no one in existence whom Allah obeys, so there is no benefit in interpreting the verse as you mentioned. Second: the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for; because if he were above him, he would be called a commander and a ruler, and would not be called an intercessor. So the term intercessor indicates that he is beneath Allah, so it is not possible to interpret His statement {obeyed} [Ghafir: 18] as applying to someone above Him. So the meaning is that they have no intercessor who is granted. The third proof: His statement, the Most High: {And before the coming of a Day in which there is no sale nor friendship nor intercession} [Al-Baqarah: 254]. The apparent meaning of this verse denies all intercessions. The fourth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And the wrongdoers have no helpers} [Al-Baqarah: 270]. The intercessor is undoubtedly one of the helpers. The fifth proof: His statement, the Most High, describing the wicked: {Indeed the wicked are in a blaze. They will burn therein on the Day of Recompense, and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 14-16]. If intercession were accepted on behalf of sinners, either in removing punishment or in bringing them out of the Fire after entering it, then His statement {and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 16] would be contrary. The sixth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And they cannot intercede except for him whom He approves} [Al-Anbiya': 28]. The transgressor is not approved, so intercession for him must be denied. The seventh proof: His statement, the Most High: {Those who bear the Throne and those around it glorify the praise of their Lord and believe in Him} [Ghafir: 7] up to His statement: {and followed Your way} [Ghafir: 7]. If intercession were obtained for the transgressor before repentance, then the restriction by the condition of repentance in His statement: {So forgive those who repent and follow Your way} [Ghafir: 7] would be in vain. The eighth proof: The community is agreed that they say: O Allah, make us among the people of the intercession of Muhammad, peace be upon him. If eligibility for intercession were only for the people of major sins, then the meaning of this supplication would be: O Allah, make us among the people of major sins and among the wicked. And it is known that this is false. And the answer to all these specious arguments is one word: that your proofs for denying intercession must be general in persons and times; otherwise they would not include the disputed matter. And our proofs for affirming intercession must be specific in persons and times, because we do not affirm intercession on behalf of all persons, nor do we affirm it at all times. So it is established that our proofs are specific and your proofs are general, and the specific takes precedence over the general, so the weight is on our side. As for the detailed answers, they are mentioned in 'Al-Tafsir al-Kabir'.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and a general answer concerning intercession (shafa'a). Raazi responds to seven additional proofs (hujaj) from the opponents (likely the Mu'tazila) who deny intercession for sinners, and then gives a methodological rebuttal. He begins with a continuation of an earlier discussion: the previous proof is handled by stating that the general wording ('umum al-lafz) is the criterion, not the specific cause. Then for the second earlier proof, he gives two responses: first, even if the verse is specified, its specification only concerns increasing good deeds, so it remains evidence for other matters; second, the purpose is intimidation (takhwif), which requires not removing punishment, not the lack of increase. Then he lists seven proofs from the Qur'an that the opponents use to deny intercession: the second proof is from Surah Ghafir 18; he explains that wrongdoers include disbelievers and transgressors, and responds to the objection that the verse only denies the intercessor being 'obeyed' but not 'accepted in speech'. He gives two answers: every rational person knows none are obeyed by Allah, so that interpretation yields no benefit; and the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for, so 'obeyed' cannot mean the intercessor is above Allah, but rather that no intercessor is granted their request. The third proof is from Al-Baqarah 254 which denies all intercessions. The fourth proof from Al-Baqarah 270 equates intercessors with helpers, which wrongdoers lack. The fifth proof from Al-Infitar 14-16 asserts that the wicked will never leave the Fire, contradicting intercession. The sixth proof from Al-Anbiya' 28 restricts intercession to those Allah approves, and the transgressor is not approved. The seventh proof from Ghafir 7 shows that intercession is tied to repentance. The eighth proof is a consensus argument: the people ask to be among the people of intercession, but if intercession were only for major sinners, that would be absurd. Finally, Raazi gives a single comprehensive answer: the opponents' proofs for denying intercession must be universal in persons and times, but the matter under dispute is specific; the proofs for affirming intercession are specific, and specific (khas) takes precedence over general ('amm). This methodological point shifts the burden of proof. The detailed responses are referred to his larger commentary.

مُطَاع
ظالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse only denies an intercessor who is obeyed in the sense of being a superior, allowing for an intercessor whose request is accepted without being obeyed.
Correction: Razi shows that 'obeyed' in this context means the intercessor's request is granted, as the intercessor is beneath Allah, so the verse denies any effective intercessor for wrongdoers.

Checkpoint
What is the second answer Razi gives to the objection about the word 'obeyed'?
A) The intercessor is above Allah, so 'obeyed' is impossible.
B) The intercessor is beneath Allah, so 'obeyed' means his request is granted.
C) The verse is abrogated by other verses.
D) The word 'obeyed' refers to angels, not humans.

Key Takeaway
Razi uses Surah Ghafir 18 to affirm that wrongdoers have no effective intercessor, and cleverly refutes the objection by analyzing the meaning of 'obeyed' in context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to stand before Allah tomorrow, would you be counted among the wrongdoers this verse describes? What hope do you have outside of Allah's mercy? This verse strips away false hopes—are you willing to let it strip yours?
?
Do you ever rely on the intercession of a saint, a scholar, or even your own good deeds as if they could compel Allah? This verse says the intercessor is beneath Allah and only effective if He grants. Does your heart place anyone in a position of authority over Allah? Repent of that today.
?
Razi's argument reveals that intercession is entirely subordinate to Allah's will. Have you been living as if your sins are automatically forgiven because of someone's status? Confront that assumption now. Will you change your relationship with sin and repentance?

Three Short Proofs: No Intercession on That Day
Razi presents three concise Qur'anic proofs against intercession: no intercession day, no helpers, and eternal stay in Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses three concise Qur'anic verses to argue that intercession is generally negated for sinners on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
Three verses collectively deny any form of intercession for wrongdoers.

Razi continues listing proofs from the Qur'an that opponents use to deny intercession. The third proof cites a verse that explicitly mentions 'no intercession' on a specific day. The fourth equates intercessors with helpers, which wrongdoers lack. The fifth argues that the wicked will forever remain in Hell, contradicting intercession. This lesson covers these three short but powerful proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read all three proofs
Read the Arabic and translation for the third, fourth, and fifth proofs together. Notice how each verse provides a different angle.
2
Analyze the third proof (Surah Al-Baqarah 254)
This verse states that on a certain day there will be no sale, friendship, or intercession. Razi says its apparent meaning negates all intercessions.
3
Analyze the fourth proof (Surah Al-Baqarah 270)
The verse says wrongdoers have no helpers. Razi argues that an intercessor is a helper, so this implies no intercessor for them.
4
Analyze the fifth proof (Surah Al-Infitar 14-16)
The verses state the wicked will burn in Hell and not be absent from it. If intercession could remove them or reduce punishment, this promise would be broken.
5
Reflect on the cumulative force
Consider how these three independent proofs strengthen the case against intercession for sinners.

المسألة السابعة والثلاثون
وأيضًا فهذه الآية تنفي مطلق الشفاعة والمعتزلة يقولون بإثبات هذه الشفاعة في باب زيادة المنافع
لأنا نجيب عن الأول بأن المذهب الصحيح أن العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب.
وعن الثاني من وجهين:
الأول: أن الآية هب أنها صارت مخصوصة إلا أن خصوصها في زيادة الحسنات فتبقى حجة فيما عداها.
الثاني: أن المقصود من هذه الآية التخويف والتخويف إنما يحصل بعدم إسقاط العقاب لا بعدم زيادة الحسنات، وهذا يدل على أن هذه الآية مختصة بأن الشفاعات لا تأثير لها يوم القيامة في إسقاط العقوبات.
الحجة الثانية: قوله تعالى: ﴿مَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعٍ يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] والظالم من يفعل الظلم، فيدخل تحته الكافر والفاسق.
لا يقال: هذا ينفي كون الشفيع مطاعًا، ولا ينفي كونه مقبول القول.
لأنا نقول: الجواب عنه من وجهين:
الأول: أن كل عاقل يعلم أنه ليس في الوجود أحد يطيعه الله تعالى، فلا يكون في حمل الآية على ما ذكرتم فائدة.
الثاني: أن الشفيع دون المشفوع إليه؛ لأنه لو كان فوقه يسمى أمرًا وحاكمًا، ولا يسمى شفيعًا، فلفظ الشفيع أفاد كونه دون الله تعالى فلم يمكن حمل قوله ﴿يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] على من فوقه فكان المراد أنه ليس لهم شفيع يجاب.
الحجة الثالثة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمِن قَبْلِ أَن يَأْتِيَ يَوْمٌ لَّا بَيْعٌ فِيهِ وَلَا خُلَّةٌ وَلَا شَفَاعَةٌ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٤] ظاهر هذه الآية ينفي جميع الشفاعات.
الحجة الرابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ أَنصَارٍ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٠] والشفيع لا شك أنه من الأنصار.
الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى في صفة الفساق: ﴿وَإِنَّ الْفُجَّارَ لَفِي جَحِيمٍ يَصْلَوْنَهَا يَوْمَ الدِّينِ وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٤-١٦] ولو كانت الشفاعة مقبولة في حق العصاة إما في إسقاط العقاب أو في الإخراج من النار بعد الدخول فيها لكان قوله: ﴿وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٦] خلفًا.
الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَنفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَىٰ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢٨] والفاسق ليس بمرتضى فوجب نفي الشفاعة عنه.
الحجة السابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ الْعَرْشَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ يُسَبِّحُونَ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّهِمْ وَيُؤْمِنُونَ بِهِ﴾ [غافر: ٧] إلى قوله: ﴿وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] ولو كانت الشفاعة حاصلة للفاسق قبل التوبة لكان التقييد بقيد التوبة في قوله: ﴿فَاغْفِرْ لِلَّذِينَ تَابُوا وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] عبثًا.
الحجة الثامنة: أجمعت الأمة على أنهم يقولون: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل شفاعة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، ولو لم تحصل أهلية الشفاعة إلا لأهل الكبائر لكان معنى هذا السؤال: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل الكبائر ومن الفساق ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل.
والجواب عن جملة هذه الشبهات بحرف واحد وهو أن دلائلكم في نفي الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون عامة في الأشخاص والأوقات، وإلا لم يدخل محل الخلاف فيها، ودلائلنا في إثبات الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون خاصة في الأشخاص والأوقات؛ لأنا لا نثبت الشفاعة في حق كل الأشخاص ولا نثبتها أيضًا في جميع الأوقات، فثبت أنه لا بد أن تكون دلائلنا خاصة ودلائلكم عامة والخاص مقدم على العام فكان الترجيح من جانبنا، وأما الأجوبة المفصلة فمذكورة في "التفسير الكبير".
The thirty-seventh issue. And also, this verse denies intercession absolutely, and the Mu'tazila affirm this intercession in the matter of increasing benefits. For we reply to the first objection: The correct position is that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not to the specificity of the cause. And to the second objection in two ways: First: that even if the verse were specified, its specification is in increasing good deeds, so it remains a proof regarding other than that. Second: that the purpose of this verse is intimidation, and intimidation only occurs by not removing punishment, not by not increasing good deeds. This indicates that this verse is specific that intercessions have no effect on the Day of Resurrection in removing punishments. The second proof: His statement, the Most High: {For the wrongdoers there is no friend and no intercessor to be obeyed} [Ghafir: 18]. The wrongdoer is one who commits wrongdoing, so it includes the disbeliever and the transgressor. It cannot be said: This denies the intercessor being obeyed, but does not deny him being accepted in speech. For we say: The answer to it is in two ways: First: every rational person knows that there is no one in existence whom Allah obeys, so there is no benefit in interpreting the verse as you mentioned. Second: the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for; because if he were above him, he would be called a commander and a ruler, and would not be called an intercessor. So the term intercessor indicates that he is beneath Allah, so it is not possible to interpret His statement {obeyed} [Ghafir: 18] as applying to someone above Him. So the meaning is that they have no intercessor who is granted. The third proof: His statement, the Most High: {And before the coming of a Day in which there is no sale nor friendship nor intercession} [Al-Baqarah: 254]. The apparent meaning of this verse denies all intercessions. The fourth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And the wrongdoers have no helpers} [Al-Baqarah: 270]. The intercessor is undoubtedly one of the helpers. The fifth proof: His statement, the Most High, describing the wicked: {Indeed the wicked are in a blaze. They will burn therein on the Day of Recompense, and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 14-16]. If intercession were accepted on behalf of sinners, either in removing punishment or in bringing them out of the Fire after entering it, then His statement {and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 16] would be contrary. The sixth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And they cannot intercede except for him whom He approves} [Al-Anbiya': 28]. The transgressor is not approved, so intercession for him must be denied. The seventh proof: His statement, the Most High: {Those who bear the Throne and those around it glorify the praise of their Lord and believe in Him} [Ghafir: 7] up to His statement: {and followed Your way} [Ghafir: 7]. If intercession were obtained for the transgressor before repentance, then the restriction by the condition of repentance in His statement: {So forgive those who repent and follow Your way} [Ghafir: 7] would be in vain. The eighth proof: The community is agreed that they say: O Allah, make us among the people of the intercession of Muhammad, peace be upon him. If eligibility for intercession were only for the people of major sins, then the meaning of this supplication would be: O Allah, make us among the people of major sins and among the wicked. And it is known that this is false. And the answer to all these specious arguments is one word: that your proofs for denying intercession must be general in persons and times; otherwise they would not include the disputed matter. And our proofs for affirming intercession must be specific in persons and times, because we do not affirm intercession on behalf of all persons, nor do we affirm it at all times. So it is established that our proofs are specific and your proofs are general, and the specific takes precedence over the general, so the weight is on our side. As for the detailed answers, they are mentioned in 'Al-Tafsir al-Kabir'.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and a general answer concerning intercession (shafa'a). Raazi responds to seven additional proofs (hujaj) from the opponents (likely the Mu'tazila) who deny intercession for sinners, and then gives a methodological rebuttal. He begins with a continuation of an earlier discussion: the previous proof is handled by stating that the general wording ('umum al-lafz) is the criterion, not the specific cause. Then for the second earlier proof, he gives two responses: first, even if the verse is specified, its specification only concerns increasing good deeds, so it remains evidence for other matters; second, the purpose is intimidation (takhwif), which requires not removing punishment, not the lack of increase. Then he lists seven proofs from the Qur'an that the opponents use to deny intercession: the second proof is from Surah Ghafir 18; he explains that wrongdoers include disbelievers and transgressors, and responds to the objection that the verse only denies the intercessor being 'obeyed' but not 'accepted in speech'. He gives two answers: every rational person knows none are obeyed by Allah, so that interpretation yields no benefit; and the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for, so 'obeyed' cannot mean the intercessor is above Allah, but rather that no intercessor is granted their request. The third proof is from Al-Baqarah 254 which denies all intercessions. The fourth proof from Al-Baqarah 270 equates intercessors with helpers, which wrongdoers lack. The fifth proof from Al-Infitar 14-16 asserts that the wicked will never leave the Fire, contradicting intercession. The sixth proof from Al-Anbiya' 28 restricts intercession to those Allah approves, and the transgressor is not approved. The seventh proof from Ghafir 7 shows that intercession is tied to repentance. The eighth proof is a consensus argument: the people ask to be among the people of intercession, but if intercession were only for major sinners, that would be absurd. Finally, Raazi gives a single comprehensive answer: the opponents' proofs for denying intercession must be universal in persons and times, but the matter under dispute is specific; the proofs for affirming intercession are specific, and specific (khas) takes precedence over general ('amm). This methodological point shifts the burden of proof. The detailed responses are referred to his larger commentary.

What is the logical consequence Razi draws from the fifth proof (Surah Al-Infitar 14-16)?
A) Intercession can only happen after the Day of Judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If on that Day there is no intercession, no friendship, and no sale, what are you personally relying on for salvation right now? Are you investing in deeds that will stand alone, or are you hoping someone else will save you?
?
The fourth proof says wrongdoers have no helpers. In what specific ways do you depend on others—scholars, saints, or even your family—to speak for you on the Day of Judgment? How does this verse challenge that dependence and turn you back to Allah alone?

Sixth and Seventh Proofs: Approval and Repentance
Razi presents two Qur'anic proofs that tie intercession to divine approval and repentance, excluding sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses Surah Al-Anbiya' 28 and Surah Ghafir 7 to argue that intercession is only for those Allah approves and that intercession is linked to repentance, thus excluding sinners who do not repent.

Core Idea
Intercession is conditional on divine approval and repentance.

The opponents of intercession also cite verses that tie intercession to Allah's approval and to repentance. The sixth proof from Surah Al-Anbiya' restricts intercession to those He approves, which excludes sinners. The seventh proof from Surah Ghafir shows that angels pray for forgiveness only for those who repent. This lesson explores these two conditional proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read both proofs
Read the Arabic and translation for the sixth and seventh proofs. Notice the conditionality in each verse.
2
Analyze the sixth proof (Surah Al-Anbiya' 28)
The verse says angels cannot intercede except for those whom Allah approves. Razi argues that a transgressor is not approved, so intercession is impossible for them.
3
Analyze the seventh proof (Surah Ghafir 7)
The angels pray for forgiveness for those who repent and follow the right path. If intercession were available without repentance, this restriction would be meaningless.
4
Reflect on the conditionality
Both proofs show that intercession is not unconditional; it requires divine approval and repentance, which sinners lack.

Source Text

المسألة السابعة والثلاثون
وأيضًا فهذه الآية تنفي مطلق الشفاعة والمعتزلة يقولون بإثبات هذه الشفاعة في باب زيادة المنافع
لأنا نجيب عن الأول بأن المذهب الصحيح أن العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب.
وعن الثاني من وجهين:
الأول: أن الآية هب أنها صارت مخصوصة إلا أن خصوصها في زيادة الحسنات فتبقى حجة فيما عداها.
الثاني: أن المقصود من هذه الآية التخويف والتخويف إنما يحصل بعدم إسقاط العقاب لا بعدم زيادة الحسنات، وهذا يدل على أن هذه الآية مختصة بأن الشفاعات لا تأثير لها يوم القيامة في إسقاط العقوبات.
الحجة الثانية: قوله تعالى: ﴿مَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعٍ يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] والظالم من يفعل الظلم، فيدخل تحته الكافر والفاسق.
لا يقال: هذا ينفي كون الشفيع مطاعًا، ولا ينفي كونه مقبول القول.
لأنا نقول: الجواب عنه من وجهين:
الأول: أن كل عاقل يعلم أنه ليس في الوجود أحد يطيعه الله تعالى، فلا يكون في حمل الآية على ما ذكرتم فائدة.
الثاني: أن الشفيع دون المشفوع إليه؛ لأنه لو كان فوقه يسمى أمرًا وحاكمًا، ولا يسمى شفيعًا، فلفظ الشفيع أفاد كونه دون الله تعالى فلم يمكن حمل قوله ﴿يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] على من فوقه فكان المراد أنه ليس لهم شفيع يجاب.
الحجة الثالثة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمِن قَبْلِ أَن يَأْتِيَ يَوْمٌ لَّا بَيْعٌ فِيهِ وَلَا خُلَّةٌ وَلَا شَفَاعَةٌ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٤] ظاهر هذه الآية ينفي جميع الشفاعات.
الحجة الرابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ أَنصَارٍ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٠] والشفيع لا شك أنه من الأنصار.
الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى في صفة الفساق: ﴿وَإِنَّ الْفُجَّارَ لَفِي جَحِيمٍ يَصْلَوْنَهَا يَوْمَ الدِّينِ وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٤-١٦] ولو كانت الشفاعة مقبولة في حق العصاة إما في إسقاط العقاب أو في الإخراج من النار بعد الدخول فيها لكان قوله: ﴿وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٦] خلفًا.
الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَنفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَىٰ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢٨] والفاسق ليس بمرتضى فوجب نفي الشفاعة عنه.
الحجة السابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ الْعَرْشَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ يُسَبِّحُونَ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّهِمْ وَيُؤْمِنُونَ بِهِ﴾ [غافر: ٧] إلى قوله: ﴿وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] ولو كانت الشفاعة حاصلة للفاسق قبل التوبة لكان التقييد بقيد التوبة في قوله: ﴿فَاغْفِرْ لِلَّذِينَ تَابُوا وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] عبثًا.
الحجة الثامنة: أجمعت الأمة على أنهم يقولون: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل شفاعة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، ولو لم تحصل أهلية الشفاعة إلا لأهل الكبائر لكان معنى هذا السؤال: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل الكبائر ومن الفساق ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل.
والجواب عن جملة هذه الشبهات بحرف واحد وهو أن دلائلكم في نفي الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون عامة في الأشخاص والأوقات، وإلا لم يدخل محل الخلاف فيها، ودلائلنا في إثبات الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون خاصة في الأشخاص والأوقات؛ لأنا لا نثبت الشفاعة في حق كل الأشخاص ولا نثبتها أيضًا في جميع الأوقات، فثبت أنه لا بد أن تكون دلائلنا خاصة ودلائلكم عامة والخاص مقدم على العام فكان الترجيح من جانبنا، وأما الأجوبة المفصلة فمذكورة في "التفسير الكبير".
The thirty-seventh issue. And also, this verse denies intercession absolutely, and the Mu'tazila affirm this intercession in the matter of increasing benefits. For we reply to the first objection: The correct position is that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not to the specificity of the cause. And to the second objection in two ways: First: that even if the verse were specified, its specification is in increasing good deeds, so it remains a proof regarding other than that. Second: that the purpose of this verse is intimidation, and intimidation only occurs by not removing punishment, not by not increasing good deeds. This indicates that this verse is specific that intercessions have no effect on the Day of Resurrection in removing punishments. The second proof: His statement, the Most High: {For the wrongdoers there is no friend and no intercessor to be obeyed} [Ghafir: 18]. The wrongdoer is one who commits wrongdoing, so it includes the disbeliever and the transgressor. It cannot be said: This denies the intercessor being obeyed, but does not deny him being accepted in speech. For we say: The answer to it is in two ways: First: every rational person knows that there is no one in existence whom Allah obeys, so there is no benefit in interpreting the verse as you mentioned. Second: the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for; because if he were above him, he would be called a commander and a ruler, and would not be called an intercessor. So the term intercessor indicates that he is beneath Allah, so it is not possible to interpret His statement {obeyed} [Ghafir: 18] as applying to someone above Him. So the meaning is that they have no intercessor who is granted. The third proof: His statement, the Most High: {And before the coming of a Day in which there is no sale nor friendship nor intercession} [Al-Baqarah: 254]. The apparent meaning of this verse denies all intercessions. The fourth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And the wrongdoers have no helpers} [Al-Baqarah: 270]. The intercessor is undoubtedly one of the helpers. The fifth proof: His statement, the Most High, describing the wicked: {Indeed the wicked are in a blaze. They will burn therein on the Day of Recompense, and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 14-16]. If intercession were accepted on behalf of sinners, either in removing punishment or in bringing them out of the Fire after entering it, then His statement {and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 16] would be contrary. The sixth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And they cannot intercede except for him whom He approves} [Al-Anbiya': 28]. The transgressor is not approved, so intercession for him must be denied. The seventh proof: His statement, the Most High: {Those who bear the Throne and those around it glorify the praise of their Lord and believe in Him} [Ghafir: 7] up to His statement: {and followed Your way} [Ghafir: 7]. If intercession were obtained for the transgressor before repentance, then the restriction by the condition of repentance in His statement: {So forgive those who repent and follow Your way} [Ghafir: 7] would be in vain. The eighth proof: The community is agreed that they say: O Allah, make us among the people of the intercession of Muhammad, peace be upon him. If eligibility for intercession were only for the people of major sins, then the meaning of this supplication would be: O Allah, make us among the people of major sins and among the wicked. And it is known that this is false. And the answer to all these specious arguments is one word: that your proofs for denying intercession must be general in persons and times; otherwise they would not include the disputed matter. And our proofs for affirming intercession must be specific in persons and times, because we do not affirm intercession on behalf of all persons, nor do we affirm it at all times. So it is established that our proofs are specific and your proofs are general, and the specific takes precedence over the general, so the weight is on our side. As for the detailed answers, they are mentioned in 'Al-Tafsir al-Kabir'.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and a general answer concerning intercession (shafa'a). Raazi responds to seven additional proofs (hujaj) from the opponents (likely the Mu'tazila) who deny intercession for sinners, and then gives a methodological rebuttal. He begins with a continuation of an earlier discussion: the previous proof is handled by stating that the general wording ('umum al-lafz) is the criterion, not the specific cause. Then for the second earlier proof, he gives two responses: first, even if the verse is specified, its specification only concerns increasing good deeds, so it remains evidence for other matters; second, the purpose is intimidation (takhwif), which requires not removing punishment, not the lack of increase. Then he lists seven proofs from the Qur'an that the opponents use to deny intercession: the second proof is from Surah Ghafir 18; he explains that wrongdoers include disbelievers and transgressors, and responds to the objection that the verse only denies the intercessor being 'obeyed' but not 'accepted in speech'. He gives two answers: every rational person knows none are obeyed by Allah, so that interpretation yields no benefit; and the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for, so 'obeyed' cannot mean the intercessor is above Allah, but rather that no intercessor is granted their request. The third proof is from Al-Baqarah 254 which denies all intercessions. The fourth proof from Al-Baqarah 270 equates intercessors with helpers, which wrongdoers lack. The fifth proof from Al-Infitar 14-16 asserts that the wicked will never leave the Fire, contradicting intercession. The sixth proof from Al-Anbiya' 28 restricts intercession to those Allah approves, and the transgressor is not approved. The seventh proof from Ghafir 7 shows that intercession is tied to repentance. The eighth proof is a consensus argument: the people ask to be among the people of intercession, but if intercession were only for major sinners, that would be absurd. Finally, Raazi gives a single comprehensive answer: the opponents' proofs for denying intercession must be universal in persons and times, but the matter under dispute is specific; the proofs for affirming intercession are specific, and specific (khas) takes precedence over general ('amm). This methodological point shifts the burden of proof. The detailed responses are referred to his larger commentary.

Key Terms

فاسق

الذين يحملون العرش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think intercession is unconditional and can benefit any sinner regardless of repentance.
Correction: Both verses show intercession is conditional upon divine approval and repentance, excluding unrepentant sinners.

Checkpoint
According to the seventh proof, what would be the consequence if intercession were available for a transgressor before repentance?
A) The angels would still pray for them.
B) The condition of repentance in the angels' prayer would be meaningless.
C) The verse would be abrogated.
D) Allah would still punish them.

Key Takeaway
Intercession is not unconditional; it requires Allah's approval and repentance, which unrepentant sinners lack, making intercession for them impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you relying on the hope of intercession while continuing in a sin you have not truly repented from? What would it mean for your soul if you died in that state?
?
The angels pray for those who repent and follow Allah's way—does your life reflect that you are among them? What specific step will you take today to follow His way more closely?
?
If Allah's approval is required for intercession, and you know He disapproves of certain actions in your life, what are you waiting for? Write down one sin you are ready to abandon right now.

Unseen Matters
intermediate

Consensus Argument and the General Methodological Answer
Razi presents a consensus-based proof and the final methodological answer: specific proofs override general ones.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's eighth proof from consensus and his overarching methodological answer that specific proofs (khas) take precedence over general proofs ('amm) regarding intercession.

Core Idea
Specific proofs override general proofs in the intercession debate.

Razi concludes his presentation of proofs against intercession with a consensus-based argument: the Muslim community asks to be among the people of intercession, which implies intercession is for the righteous, not sinners. Then he delivers a powerful methodological punch: the opponents' proofs are general, but the proponents' proofs are specific, and specific always precedes general. This lesson covers the final proof and the decisive answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the eighth proof and the general answer
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the shift from individual proofs to a holistic argument.
2
Understand the eighth proof from consensus
Razi argues that the community's supplication to be among the people of intercession implies that intercession is for the righteous, not major sinners.
3
Grasp the general methodological answer
Razi states that for the opponents' proofs to work, they must be universal in persons and times. But the proponents' proofs are specific (khas). In uṣūl al-fiqh, specific precedes general.
4
Reflect on the resolution
Consider how this methodological move resolves the entire debate: the specific verses that affirm intercession (like the Prophet's intercession) override the general verses that seem to deny it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة السابعة والثلاثون
وأيضًا فهذه الآية تنفي مطلق الشفاعة والمعتزلة يقولون بإثبات هذه الشفاعة في باب زيادة المنافع
لأنا نجيب عن الأول بأن المذهب الصحيح أن العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب.
وعن الثاني من وجهين:
الأول: أن الآية هب أنها صارت مخصوصة إلا أن خصوصها في زيادة الحسنات فتبقى حجة فيما عداها.
الثاني: أن المقصود من هذه الآية التخويف والتخويف إنما يحصل بعدم إسقاط العقاب لا بعدم زيادة الحسنات، وهذا يدل على أن هذه الآية مختصة بأن الشفاعات لا تأثير لها يوم القيامة في إسقاط العقوبات.
الحجة الثانية: قوله تعالى: ﴿مَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعٍ يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] والظالم من يفعل الظلم، فيدخل تحته الكافر والفاسق.
لا يقال: هذا ينفي كون الشفيع مطاعًا، ولا ينفي كونه مقبول القول.
لأنا نقول: الجواب عنه من وجهين:
الأول: أن كل عاقل يعلم أنه ليس في الوجود أحد يطيعه الله تعالى، فلا يكون في حمل الآية على ما ذكرتم فائدة.
الثاني: أن الشفيع دون المشفوع إليه؛ لأنه لو كان فوقه يسمى أمرًا وحاكمًا، ولا يسمى شفيعًا، فلفظ الشفيع أفاد كونه دون الله تعالى فلم يمكن حمل قوله ﴿يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] على من فوقه فكان المراد أنه ليس لهم شفيع يجاب.
الحجة الثالثة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمِن قَبْلِ أَن يَأْتِيَ يَوْمٌ لَّا بَيْعٌ فِيهِ وَلَا خُلَّةٌ وَلَا شَفَاعَةٌ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٤] ظاهر هذه الآية ينفي جميع الشفاعات.
الحجة الرابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ أَنصَارٍ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٠] والشفيع لا شك أنه من الأنصار.
الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى في صفة الفساق: ﴿وَإِنَّ الْفُجَّارَ لَفِي جَحِيمٍ يَصْلَوْنَهَا يَوْمَ الدِّينِ وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٤-١٦] ولو كانت الشفاعة مقبولة في حق العصاة إما في إسقاط العقاب أو في الإخراج من النار بعد الدخول فيها لكان قوله: ﴿وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٦] خلفًا.
الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَنفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَىٰ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢٨] والفاسق ليس بمرتضى فوجب نفي الشفاعة عنه.
الحجة السابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ الْعَرْشَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ يُسَبِّحُونَ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّهِمْ وَيُؤْمِنُونَ بِهِ﴾ [غافر: ٧] إلى قوله: ﴿وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] ولو كانت الشفاعة حاصلة للفاسق قبل التوبة لكان التقييد بقيد التوبة في قوله: ﴿فَاغْفِرْ لِلَّذِينَ تَابُوا وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] عبثًا.
الحجة الثامنة: أجمعت الأمة على أنهم يقولون: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل شفاعة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، ولو لم تحصل أهلية الشفاعة إلا لأهل الكبائر لكان معنى هذا السؤال: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل الكبائر ومن الفساق ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل.
والجواب عن جملة هذه الشبهات بحرف واحد وهو أن دلائلكم في نفي الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون عامة في الأشخاص والأوقات، وإلا لم يدخل محل الخلاف فيها، ودلائلنا في إثبات الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون خاصة في الأشخاص والأوقات؛ لأنا لا نثبت الشفاعة في حق كل الأشخاص ولا نثبتها أيضًا في جميع الأوقات، فثبت أنه لا بد أن تكون دلائلنا خاصة ودلائلكم عامة والخاص مقدم على العام فكان الترجيح من جانبنا، وأما الأجوبة المفصلة فمذكورة في "التفسير الكبير".
The thirty-seventh issue. And also, this verse denies intercession absolutely, and the Mu'tazila affirm this intercession in the matter of increasing benefits. For we reply to the first objection: The correct position is that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not to the specificity of the cause. And to the second objection in two ways: First: that even if the verse were specified, its specification is in increasing good deeds, so it remains a proof regarding other than that. Second: that the purpose of this verse is intimidation, and intimidation only occurs by not removing punishment, not by not increasing good deeds. This indicates that this verse is specific that intercessions have no effect on the Day of Resurrection in removing punishments. The second proof: His statement, the Most High: {For the wrongdoers there is no friend and no intercessor to be obeyed} [Ghafir: 18]. The wrongdoer is one who commits wrongdoing, so it includes the disbeliever and the transgressor. It cannot be said: This denies the intercessor being obeyed, but does not deny him being accepted in speech. For we say: The answer to it is in two ways: First: every rational person knows that there is no one in existence whom Allah obeys, so there is no benefit in interpreting the verse as you mentioned. Second: the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for; because if he were above him, he would be called a commander and a ruler, and would not be called an intercessor. So the term intercessor indicates that he is beneath Allah, so it is not possible to interpret His statement {obeyed} [Ghafir: 18] as applying to someone above Him. So the meaning is that they have no intercessor who is granted. The third proof: His statement, the Most High: {And before the coming of a Day in which there is no sale nor friendship nor intercession} [Al-Baqarah: 254]. The apparent meaning of this verse denies all intercessions. The fourth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And the wrongdoers have no helpers} [Al-Baqarah: 270]. The intercessor is undoubtedly one of the helpers. The fifth proof: His statement, the Most High, describing the wicked: {Indeed the wicked are in a blaze. They will burn therein on the Day of Recompense, and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 14-16]. If intercession were accepted on behalf of sinners, either in removing punishment or in bringing them out of the Fire after entering it, then His statement {and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 16] would be contrary. The sixth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And they cannot intercede except for him whom He approves} [Al-Anbiya': 28]. The transgressor is not approved, so intercession for him must be denied. The seventh proof: His statement, the Most High: {Those who bear the Throne and those around it glorify the praise of their Lord and believe in Him} [Ghafir: 7] up to His statement: {and followed Your way} [Ghafir: 7]. If intercession were obtained for the transgressor before repentance, then the restriction by the condition of repentance in His statement: {So forgive those who repent and follow Your way} [Ghafir: 7] would be in vain. The eighth proof: The community is agreed that they say: O Allah, make us among the people of the intercession of Muhammad, peace be upon him. If eligibility for intercession were only for the people of major sins, then the meaning of this supplication would be: O Allah, make us among the people of major sins and among the wicked. And it is known that this is false. And the answer to all these specious arguments is one word: that your proofs for denying intercession must be general in persons and times; otherwise they would not include the disputed matter. And our proofs for affirming intercession must be specific in persons and times, because we do not affirm intercession on behalf of all persons, nor do we affirm it at all times. So it is established that our proofs are specific and your proofs are general, and the specific takes precedence over the general, so the weight is on our side. As for the detailed answers, they are mentioned in 'Al-Tafsir al-Kabir'.

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and a general answer concerning intercession (shafa'a). Raazi responds to seven additional proofs (hujaj) from the opponents (likely the Mu'tazila) who deny intercession for sinners, and then gives a methodological rebuttal. He begins with a continuation of an earlier discussion: the previous proof is handled by stating that the general wording ('umum al-lafz) is the criterion, not the specific cause. Then for the second earlier proof, he gives two responses: first, even if the verse is specified, its specification only concerns increasing good deeds, so it remains evidence for other matters; second, the purpose is intimidation (takhwif), which requires not removing punishment, not the lack of increase. Then he lists seven proofs from the Qur'an that the opponents use to deny intercession: the second proof is from Surah Ghafir 18; he explains that wrongdoers include disbelievers and transgressors, and responds to the objection that the verse only denies the intercessor being 'obeyed' but not 'accepted in speech'. He gives two answers: every rational person knows none are obeyed by Allah, so that interpretation yields no benefit; and the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for, so 'obeyed' cannot mean the intercessor is above Allah, but rather that no intercessor is granted their request. The third proof is from Al-Baqarah 254 which denies all intercessions. The fourth proof from Al-Baqarah 270 equates intercessors with helpers, which wrongdoers lack. The fifth proof from Al-Infitar 14-16 asserts that the wicked will never leave the Fire, contradicting intercession. The sixth proof from Al-Anbiya' 28 restricts intercession to those Allah approves, and the transgressor is not approved. The seventh proof from Ghafir 7 shows that intercession is tied to repentance. The eighth proof is a consensus argument: the people ask to be among the people of intercession, but if intercession were only for major sinners, that would be absurd. Finally, Raazi gives a single comprehensive answer: the opponents' proofs for denying intercession must be universal in persons and times, but the matter under dispute is specific; the proofs for affirming intercession are specific, and specific (khas) takes precedence over general ('amm). This methodological point shifts the burden of proof. The detailed responses are referred to his larger commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all verses denying intercession are absolute and cannot be reconciled with verses affirming it.
Correction: Razi shows that the affirming verses are specific in scope (e.g., only for certain persons or times), so they are reconciled with the general negating verses by the principle that specific takes precedence.

Checkpoint
What is the 'one word' answer Razi gives to all the specious arguments against intercession?
A) The verses are abrogated.
B) The specific proofs take precedence over the general.
C) The Intercession is only for disbelievers.
D) The consensus is the strongest proof.

Key Takeaway
Razi concludes that the proponents' specific proofs for intercession override the opponents' general proofs, establishing the validity of intercession for the righteous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray 'O Allah, make us among the people of the intercession of Muhammad,' do you truly intend to be among those who are worthy of it? What does your daily life reveal about your eligibility – are you actively seeking righteousness or comfortable with sin, assuming intercession will cover you? This lesson shows that the supplication itself implies a desire for righteousness, not sin. Is your du'a sincere or just a habit?
?
The lesson establishes that specific proofs override general ones. In your own life, do you allow the specific commands of Allah (e.g., prayer, charity, avoiding backbiting) to override your general excuses or desires? Do you treat the clear texts of the Qur'an and Sunnah as specific rulings that must take precedence over your own general preferences? Examine one specific command you have been neglecting – what general excuse do you use?
?
Razi's consensus argument shows that the collective practice of the ummah reflects a deep belief in intercession for the righteous. Are you truly part of that collective practice? Do you regularly and consciously ask for intercession, or do you neglect it? How does that reflect your actual trust in the Prophet's intercession? What would change in your daily worship if you deeply believed that your eligibility for intercession depends on your righteousness starting today?

Three Scriptural Proofs Against Intercession for Sinners
Razi enumerates three proofs denying intercession for sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's three scriptural proofs that intercession does not benefit sinners, including the Quranic verses and the consensus argument.

Core Idea
Scriptural texts condition intercession on divine approval and repentance, not on sin.

Razi presents three proofs from the Quran and consensus to argue that intercession is not for sinners. Each proof highlights a condition—divine approval, repentance, or worthiness—that excludes the unrepentant sinner. This lesson walks through each proof, showing their logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Read the first proof from Quran 21:28
Read the first proof carefully. Notice how Razi argues that since the sinner is not among those whom Allah approves, the verse's exception ('except for whom He approves') excludes them from intercession.
The key term is 'ارْتَضَىٰ' (approval).
2
Read the second proof from Quran 40:7
Read the second proof, which uses a conditional argument. Razi points out that the angels' prayer for forgiveness is restricted to those who repent; if intercession were for sinners without repentance, the restriction would be meaningless.
Focus on the term 'تَابُوا' (repented).
3
Read the third proof from consensus
Read the third proof based on the ummah's prayer to be made worthy of intercession. Razi argues that if only sinners were eligible, the prayer would be requesting sinfulness, which is absurd.
This is an argument from common practice.
4
Reflect on the common thread
Notice that all three proofs deny intercession to sinners by establishing conditions that sinners do not meet: divine approval, repentance, and worthiness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : قوله تعالى : ﴿وَلا يَنفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَىٰ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢٨] والفاسق ليس بمرتضى فوجب نفي الشفاعة عنه.
الحجة السابعة: قوله تعالى : ﴿الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ الْعَرْشَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ يُسَبِّحُونَ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّهِمْ وَيُؤْمِنُونَ بِهِ﴾ [غافر: ٧] إلى قوله : ﴿وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] ولو كانت الشفاعة حاصلة للفاسق قبل التوبة لكان التقييد بقيد التوبة في قوله : ﴿فَاغْفِرْ لِلَّذِينَ تَابُوا وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] عَبَثًا.
الحجة الثامنة : أجمعت الأمة على أنهم يقولون : اللهم اجعلنا من أهل شفاعة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ولو لم تحصل أهلية الشفاعة إلا لأهل الكبائر لكان معنى هذا السؤال : اللهم اجعلنا من أهل الكبائر ومن الفساق ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل.
والجواب عن جملة هذه الشبهات بحرف واحد وهو أن دلائلكم في نفي الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون عامة في الأشخاص والأوقات، وإلا لم يدخل محل الخلاف فيها، ودلائلنا في إثبات الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون خاصة في الأشخاص والأوقات ؛ لأنا لا نثبت الشفاعة في حق كل الأشخاص ولا نثبتها أيضًا في جميع الأوقات، فثبت أنه لا بد أن تكون دلائلنا خاصة ودلائلكم عامة والخاص مقدم على العام فكان الترجيح من جانبنا، وأما الأجوبة المفصلة فمذكورة في "التفسير الكبير".
The sixth proof: His saying: 'And they do not benefit except for whom He approves' [Quran 21:28]. And the sinner is not approved, so it is necessary to deny intercession for him.
The seventh proof: His saying: 'Those who bear the Throne and those around it glorify the praises of their Lord and believe in Him' [Quran 40:7] up to His saying: 'And followed Your way' [Quran 40:7]. And if intercession were obtained for the sinner before repentance, the restriction to the condition of repentance in His saying: 'So forgive those who repented and followed Your way' [Quran 40:7] would be in vain.
The eighth proof: The ummah is unanimous that they say: 'O Allah, make us among the people of the intercession of Muhammad, peace be upon him.' And if the eligibility for intercession were only for the people of major sins, the meaning of this request would be: 'O Allah, make us among the people of major sins and among the sinners,' and it is known that that is false.
The answer to all these doubts in one word: Your proofs for denying intercession must be general with respect to persons and times, otherwise the point of dispute would not be included in them. And our proofs for affirming intercession must be specific with respect to persons and times, because we do not affirm intercession for every person nor do we affirm it at all times. So it is established that our proofs must be specific and your proofs general. And the specific is given precedence over the general, so the preponderance is on our side. As for the detailed answers, they are mentioned in 'al-Tafsir al-Kabir'.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage presents three proofs against intercession for sinners and a general answer. First proof: Quran 21:28 states that intercession only benefits those whom God approves, and the sinner is not approved, so no intercession. Second proof: Quran 40:7 describes angels praying for forgiveness for those who repent and follow God's way; if intercession were granted to sinners without repentance, the condition of repentance would be superfluous. Third proof: The ummah's prayer to be made among those worthy of intercession implies worthiness is not sin; if only sinners were worthy, the prayer would be for sinfulness. Then the answer: Razi argues that the opponents' proofs must be general to cover the disputed case, while his proofs are specific. Since specific evidence overrides general, his side is preponderant. Detailed answers are deferred to his Tafsir al-Kabir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that intercession is unconditional and available to all sinners regardless of repentance.
Correction: Razi shows that intercession is conditional upon divine approval, repentance, and worthiness, as evidenced by Quranic verses and consensus.

Checkpoint
What is the logic behind the seventh proof from Quran 40:7?
A) The verse explicitly forbids intercession for sinners.
B) The restriction to repentance proves that intercession is not for sinners before repentance.
C) The angels pray for all believers regardless of sin.
D) Intercession only benefit those who carry the throne.

Key Takeaway
Razi uses three proofs—two from the Quran and one from consensus—to show that intercession is not for unrepentant sinners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that the Prophet's intercession is a safety net for your sins, without actively pursuing repentance? What would it mean for you to truly seek divine approval today?
?
When you recite the prayer 'make us among the people of his intercession', do you sincerely consider the condition of worthiness, or do you treat it as a mere formula? How can you align your life with that condition?
?
If you knew that intercession is only for those who repent and follow God's way, what sin or habit have you been tolerating that needs urgent repentance? Will you take a concrete step to turn back today?
